            <a href="#overview">                                    <h2 class="_orange">                                        Overview                                    </h2>                                </a>                                <p class="_lead">                                    This year, over 100,000 developers told us how they learn, build their careers, which tools they’re using, and what they want in a job.                                </p>                            </div>                        </div>                    </div>                    <div class="section-content">                            <p>Each year, we ask the developer community about everything from their favorite technologies to their job preferences. This year marks the eighth year we’ve published our Annual Developer Survey results—with the largest number of respondents yet. Over 100,000 developers took the 30-minute survey this past January.</p>                            <p>This year, we covered a few new topics ranging from artificial intelligence to ethics in coding. Here are a few of the top takeaways from this year’s results:</p>                            <ul>                                <li>DevOps and machine learning are important trends in the software industry today. Languages and frameworks associated with these kinds of works are on the rise, and developers working in these areas command the highest salaries.</li>                                <li>Only tiny fractions of developers say that they would write unethical code or that they have no obligation to consider the ethical implications of code, but beyond that, respondents see a lot of ethical gray. Developers are not sure how they would report ethical problems, and have differing ideas about who ultimately is responsible for unethical code.</li>                                <li>Developers are overall optimistic about the possibilities that artificial intelligence offers, but are not in agreement about what the dangers of AI are.</li>                                <li>Python has risen in the ranks of programming languages on our survey, surpassing C# in popularity this year, much like it surpassed PHP last year.</li>                                <li>When assessing a prospective job, different kinds of developers apply different sets of priorities. Women say their highest priorities are company culture and opportunities for professional development, while men say their highest priorities are compensation and working with specific technologies.</li>                            </ul>                            <p>Want to dive into the results yourself? In a few weeks, we’ll make the anonymized results of the survey available for download under the <a href="https://opendatacommons.org/licenses/odbl/1.0/" target="_blank" rel="noopener noreferrer">Open Database License (ODbL)</a>. We look forward to seeing what you find!</p>                                            </div>                </section>                <section id="developer-profile">                    <div                      <a href="#developer-profile">                                    <h2 class="_orange">                                        Developer Profile                                    </h2>                                </a>                                <p class="_lead">                                    What we know about the developers who are writing the script for the future                                </p>                            </div>                        </div>                    </div>                    <div class="section-content"><div class="tab-pane" role="tabpanel" id="profileGeo-providence">                <div id="highmap-providence" class="highmap-size"></div>            </div>        </div>    </div><p>Each month, about 50 million people visit Stack Overflow to learn, share, and build their careers. We estimate that 21 million of these people are professional developers and university-level students.</p><p>Our estimate of professional developers comes from the things people <a href="https://kevinmontrose.com/2015/01/27/providence-machine-learning-at-stack-exchange/">read and do</a> when they visit Stack Overflow. We collect data on user activity to help surface jobs we think you might find interesting and questions we think you can answer. You can <a href="https://stackoverflow.com/users/prediction-data">download</a> and clear this data at any time.</p><div class="subsection-head" id="developer-roles">    <h3 class="_inline-block"> back-end developers, and about 20% consider themselves mobile developers. The median number of developer type identifications per respondent is 2, and the most common pairs are combinations of back-end, front-end, and full-stack developer. Pairs that are highly correlated are database administrator and system administrator, DevOps specialist and system administrator, and designer and front-end developer.</p>    <h4 id="developer-profile-contributing-to-open-source"><a href="#developer-profile-contributing-to-open-source">Contributing to Open Source</a></h4>    <div class="tab-container">        <div         </div>    </div>        <sub class="_muted _line-top">            87,450 responses        </sub>            </div>    </div><p>Almost half of professional developers on Stack Overflow contribute to open source projects. Involvement in open source varies with language. Over 70% of developers who work with Rust, Julia, and Clojure contribute to open source, while less than 40% of developers who work with VBA, VB.NET, and C# do so.</p>    <h4 id="developer-profile-coding-as-a-hobby"><a href="#developer-profile-coding-as-a-hobby">Coding as a Hobby</a></h4>    <div class="tab-container">        <div class="tab-inner-container">            <ul class="nav nav-tabs" role="tablist">                    <li class="active"><a href="#developer-profile-developer-roles-all-respondents2" role="tab" data-toggle="tab">All Respondents</a></li>                    <li><a href="#developer-profile-developer-roles-professional-developers2" role="tab" data-toggle="tab">Professional Developers</a></li>            </ul>        </div>    </div>    <div class="_muted _line-top">            87,450 responses        </sub>            </div>    </div><p>Many developers work on code outside of work. Over 80% of our respondents say that they code as a hobby. Other interests or responsibilities outside of software don't seem to reduce developers' interest in coding as a hobby. Those who said they are parents or have other caretaking responsibilities, those who exercise daily, or those who spend the most time outside were slightly <em>more</em> likely to code as a hobby than other groups.</p><div class="subsection-head" id="experience">    <h3 class="_inline-block">        <svg id="Layer_1" data-name="Layer 1" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 48.125 href="#experience">Experience</a>    </h3></div>    <h4 id="developer-profile-years-since-learning-to-code"><a href="#developer-profile-years-since-learning-to-code">Years Since Learning to Code</a></h4>    <div class="tab-container">        <div class="tab-inner-container">            <ul class="nav nav-tabs" role="tablist">                    <li class="active"><a or less. Developers who work with languages such as Cobol and Perl have the most years of professional coding experience, while developers who work with languages like Matlab, Haskell, and Kotlin have the fewest.</p>    <h4 id="developer-profile-years-of-professional-coding-experience-by-developer-type"><a href="#developer-profile-years-of-professional-coding-experience-by-developer-type">Years of  <sub class="_muted _line-top">            Mean of 77,078 responses        </sub><p>Developers who work in different areas of software development have different average amounts of experience. DevOps specialists and developers who code for desktop and enterprise applications have the most experience. DevOps as a discipline and professional identity is relatively new, but the people working in this field are highly experienced. Game/graphics developers and mobile developers have the fewest years of experience.</p><div class="subsection-head" id="education">    <h3 class="_inline-block">        <svg id="Layer_1" This proportion is somewhat higher in currently enrolled students, and the proportion of respondents majoring in other engineering disciplines like electrical and mechanical engineering is lower among current students than among professionals.</p>    <h4 id="developer-profile-other-types-of-education"><a href="#developer-profile-other-types-of-education">Other Types of Education</a></h4>    <div learners; almost 90% of all developers say they have taught themselves a new language, framework, or tool outside of their formal education. Among professional developers, almost half say they have taken an online course like a MOOC, and about a quarter have participated in a hackathon.</p>    <h4 Q&amp;A when learning something new. Additionally, developers understand the value of good documentation, as over 80% also use documentation as a resource when learning.</p>    <h4 id="developer-profile-why-do-developers-participate-in-hackathons"><a href="#developer-profile-why-do-developers-participate-in-hackathons">Why Do Developers Participate in Hackathons?</a></h4>    <div class="bar-set">                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Because I find it enjoyable</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 100%;" class="">                        <span>76.3%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">To improve my general technical skills or programming ability</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 86.6796%;" class="">                        <span>66.1%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">To improve my knowledge of a specific programming language, framework, or other technology</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 67.1583%;" class="outside">                        <span>51.2%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">To improve my ability to work on a team with other programmers</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 39.2773%;" class="outside">                        <span>30.0%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">To build my professional network</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 36.0416%;" class="outside">                        <span>27.5%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">To help me find new job opportunities</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 27.2788%;" class="outside">                        <span>20.8%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">To win prizes or cash awards</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 24.7473%;" class="outside">                        <span>18.9%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>    </div>        <sub class="_muted _line-top">            25,691 responses; select all that apply        </sub><p>Among the respondents who said they have participated in hackathons or online coding competitions, their number one reason for engaging is that they find them enjoyable. These are also opportunities for learning, both general and specific.</p>    <h4 id="developer-profile-finding-a-job-after-bootcamp"><a href="#developer-profile-finding-a-job-after-bootcamp">Finding a Job After Bootcamp</a></h4>    <div class="bar-set">                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">I already had a full-time job as a developer when I began the program</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 100%;" class="">                        <span>45.5%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Immediately after graduating</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 35.8678%;" class="outside">                        <span>16.3%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Less than a month</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 16.3967%;" class="outside">                        <span>7.5%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">One to three months</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 22.0827%;" class="outside">                        <span>10.0%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Four to six months</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 11.4711%;" class="outside">                        <span>5.2%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Six months to a year</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 7.9008%;" class="outside">                        <span>3.6%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Longer than a year</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 6.9753%;" class="outside">                        <span>3.2%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">I haven’t gotten a developer job</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 19.2066%;" class="outside">                        <span>8.7%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>    </div>        <sub class="_muted _line-top">            6,652 responses        </sub><p>Bootcamps are typically perceived as a way for newcomers to transition into a career as a software developer, but according to our survey, many participants in coding bootcamps were already working as developers. Almost half of our respondents who said they went to a coding bootcamp said they were already working as developers; these developers are likely updating their skills and moving to new areas of the tech industry. Of other bootcamp participants, the most common outcome is to find a job immediately or soon after graduating.</p><div class="subsection-head" id="demographics">    <h3 class="_inline-block">        <sub class="_muted _line-top">            13,985 responses; select all that apply        </sub>            </div>    </div><p>We asked our respondents about their gender identity, and found that over 90% of our respondents are male. According to Quantcast, women account for about 10% of Stack Overflow’s US traffic; this year 9% of US survey respondents are women. We had survey participation at almost the rate we would expect from our traffic, although such a low percentage points to problems with inclusion in the tech industry in general and Stack Overflow in particular. In regions including the United States, India, and the UK, women are represented at higher levels among students than among professional developers.</p><p>This year, 0.7% of respondents identified as transgender men or women. The gender identifications are select all that apply, so transgender men and women are included in the categories shown here.</p>    <h4 id="developer-profile-race-and-ethnicity"><a     </div>            <div class="tab-pane fade" id="developer-profile-demographics-physical-differences" role="tabpanel">                    <div class="bar-set">                <div class="bar-row">       </sub>            </div>    </div><p>We know developers can experience many forms of disability and difference, from mental health challenges to physical disability. Mental health issues like depression and anxiety are particularly common among our respondents. In the United States, almost 20% of respondents said they deal with either or both.</p>    <h4 id="developer-profile-experience-and-gender"><a        </sub>            </div>    </div><p>We find differences among developers by gender in our survey responses. For example, twice as many women than men have been coding two years or less, evidence for the shifting demographics of coding as a profession. Also, developers who identify as transgender men or women or of non-binary gender contribute to open source at higher rates (58% and 60%, respectively) than developers who identify as men or women overall (45% and 33%.)</p>    <h4 id="developer-profile-developer-role-and-gender"><a href="#developer-profile-developer-role-and-gender">Developer Role and Gender</a></h4>        <img src="https://cdn.sstatic.net/insights/Img/Survey/2018/devtype_ratio-1.svg?v=148511abf34f" style="width: 100%;" />        <sub class="_muted _line-top">            The dashed line shows the average ratio of men&#39;s to women&#39;s participation        </sub><p>We see varying representation by men and women in different developer roles on our survey. All categories have dramatically more developers who identify as men than women but the ratio of men to women varies. Developers who are educators or academic researchers are about 10 times more likely to be men than women, while developers who are system admins or DevOps specialists are 25-30 times more likely to be men than women. Women have the highest representation as academics, QA developers, data scientists, and designers.</p>    <h4 id="developer-profile-age"><a href="#developer-profile-age">Age</a></h4>    <div style="fill:none;stroke:#1060e1;stroke-linecap:round;stroke-linejoin:round"/></g></svg>        <a href="#connection-and-competition">Connection and Competition</a>    </h3></div>    <h4 id="developer-profile-kinship-competition-and-self-evaluation"><a href="#developer-profile-kinship-competition-and-self-evaluation">Kinship, Competition, and Self-Evaluation</a></h4>    <div class="bar-set">                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">I feel a sense of kinship or connection to other developers</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 100%;" class="">                        <span>3.6</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">I think of myself as competing with my peers</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 74.5829%;" class="outside">                        <span>2.7</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">I&#39;m not as good at programming as most of my peers</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 61.3441%;" class="outside">                        <span>2.2</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>    </div>        <sub class="_muted _line-top">            68,577 responses; agreement on a 1-5 scale, from strongly disagree to strongly agree        </sub><p>We asked how much respondents agree or disagree with several statements about their place in the developer community. Overall 70% of developers agree or strongly agree that they feel a sense of connection with other developers. Developers are overall confident about their own skills compared to their peers, with only 18% agreeing or strongly agreeing that they are not as good at programming as their colleagues.</p>    <h4 id="developer-profile-experience-and-belonging"><a href="#developer-profile-experience-and-belonging">Experience and Belonging</a></h4>        <img src="https://cdn.sstatic.net/insights/Img/Survey/2018/kinship-1.svg?v=9f87a518299b" style="width: 100%;" /><p>Respondents' feelings on how much they belong and how they stack up to their peers change with how much experience they have. More experienced developers feel more connected, more confident, and less competitive. Notice that feeling less skilled drops quickly with experience while feeling less competitive drops more gradually and continues to drop into the second decade of coding experience.</p><div class="subsection-head" id="life-outside-work">    <h3 class="_inline-block">        <svg id="Layer_1" data-name="Layer 1" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 51 47"><title>Life-Outside-of-Work</title><line x1="0.69481" y1="45.9797" x2="50.30519" y2="45.9797" style="fill:none;stroke:#1060e1;stroke-miterlimit:10"/><line x1="14.64773" y1="45.9797" x2="14.64773" y2="9.54708" style="fill:none;stroke:#1060e1;stroke-miterlimit:10"/><path d="M7.67127,23.5c0-7.27776,1.55033-13.17775,6.97646-13.17775s6.97646,5.9,6.97646,13.17775" style="fill:none;stroke:#1060e1;stroke-miterlimit:10"/><path d="M1.47,23.5H27.82549A13.17776,13.17776,0,0,0,1.47,23.5Z" style="fill:none;stroke:#1060e1;stroke-miterlimit:10"/><polyline points="18.524 41.329 38.678 41.329 43.329 45.98" style="fill:none;stroke:#1060e1;stroke-miterlimit:10"/><line x1="23.17451" y1="41.32873" x2="18.52354" y2="45.9797" style="fill:none;stroke:#1060e1;stroke-miterlimit:10"/><line x1="26.27516" y1="41.32873" x2="19.2987" y2="34.35227" style="fill:none;stroke:#1060e1;stroke-miterlimit:10"/><polyline points="34.027 41.329 30.926 38.228 23.175 38.228" style="fill:none;stroke:#1060e1;stroke-miterlimit:10"/><path d="M33.25162,8.77192c4.651,0,5.42613,3.10065,5.42613,3.10065s.77517-3.10065,5.42614-3.10065" style="fill:none;stroke:#1060e1;stroke-miterlimit:10"/><line x1="38.67775" y1="11.87257" x2="38.67775" y2="12.64773" style="fill:none;stroke:#1060e1;stroke-miterlimit:10"/><path d="M22.72073,9.54181a13.95562,13.95562,0,1,1,4.71942,16.7666" style="fill:none;stroke:#1060e1;stroke-miterlimit:10"/></svg>        <a href="#life-outside-work">Life Outside Work</a>    </h3></div>    <h4 id="developer-profile-children-and-other-dependents"><a href="#developer-profile-children-and-other-dependents">Children and Other Dependents</a></h4>    <div class="bar-set">                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">No</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 100%;" class="">                        <span>71.1%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Yes</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 40.7347%;" class="outside">                        <span>28.9%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>    </div>        <sub class="_muted _line-top">            62,596 responses        </sub><p>This year we asked respondents if they have children or other dependents that they care for, and about a quarter of respondents say that they do. We asked in a free response question what these developers do for dependent care during work hours, and our respondents talked about options like school, their spouses/partners, and daycare.</p><p>The developers who said they do not have dependents to care for are younger on average than those who do. Over 30% of the developers without dependents are younger than 25, while only 5% of those with dependents are younger than 25. Almost 60% of developers with 10 or more years of professional coding experience have children or other dependents.</p>    <h4 id="developer-profile-what-time-do-developers-wake-up"><a href="#developer-profile-what-time-do-developers-wake-up">What Time Do Developers Wake Up?</a></h4>    <div class="bar-set">                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Before 5:00 AM</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 8.1411%;" class="outside">                        <span>2.4%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Between 5:00 - 6:00 AM</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 41.9859%;" class="outside">                        <span>12.4%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Between 6:01 - 7:00 AM</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 95.6329%;" class="">                        <span>28.2%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Between 7:01 - 8:00 AM</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 100%;" class="">                        <span>29.5%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Between 8:01 - 9:00 AM</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 49.8445%;" class="outside">                        <span>14.7%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Between 9:01 - 10:00 AM</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 16.2493%;" class="outside">                        <span>4.8%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Between 10:01 - 11:00 AM</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 4.8%;" class="outside">                        <span>1.4%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Between 11:01 AM - 12:00 PM</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 1.8211%;" class="outside">                        <span>0.5%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">After 12:01 PM</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 1.4164%;" class="outside">                        <span>0.4%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">I work night shifts</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 1.5387%;" class="outside">                        <span>0.5%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">I do not have a set schedule</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 18.0799%;" class="outside">                        <span>5.3%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>    </div>        <sub class="_muted _line-top">            72,146 responses        </sub><p>We are confident that most developers have pulled a late night here and there, but most of our respondents say they are up by 8am.</p>    <h4 id="developer-profile-how-much-time-do-developers-spend-on-a-computer"><a href="#developer-profile-how-much-time-do-developers-spend-on-a-computer">How Much Time Do Developers Spend on a Computer?</a></h4>    <div class="bar-set">                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Less than 1 hour</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 0.4791%;" class="outside">                        <span>0.3%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">1 - 4 hours</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 6.1844%;" class="outside">                        <span>3.3%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">5 - 8 hours</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 58.105%;" class="outside">                        <span>30.6%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">9 - 12 hours</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 100%;" class="">                        <span>52.7%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Over 12 hours</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 25.1401%;" class="outside">                        <span>13.2%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>    </div>        <sub class="_muted _line-top">            72,133 responses        </sub><p>Our respondents include people who code as professionals, students, and hobbyists. The overwhelmingly majority spend large fractions of their waking hours on a typical day with their desktops and laptops.</p>    <h4 id="developer-profile-how-much-time-do-developers-spend-outside"><a href="#developer-profile-how-much-time-do-developers-spend-outside">How Much Time Do Developers Spend Outside?</a></h4>    <div class="bar-set">                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Less than 30 minutes</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 40.3879%;" class="outside">                        <span>15.6%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">30 - 59 minutes</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 86.3754%;" class="">                        <span>33.3%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">1 - 2 hours</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 100%;" class="">                        <span>38.6%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">3 - 4 hours</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 25.86%;" class="outside">                        <span>10.0%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Over 4 hours</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 6.5676%;" class="outside">                        <span>2.5%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>    </div>        <sub class="_muted _line-top">            72,024 responses        </sub><p>Developers get outside for recreation, commuting, or other reasons. About half of our respondents spend an hour or more outside a day.</p>    <h4 id="developer-profile-healthy-habits"><a href="#developer-profile-healthy-habits">Healthy Habits</a></h4>    <div class="tab-container">        <div class="tab-inner-container">            <ul class="nav nav-tabs" role="tablist">                    <li class="active"><a href="#developer-profile-life-outside-work-how-often-do-developers-skip-meals-to-be-productive" role="tab" data-toggle="tab">How Often Do Developers Skip Meals To Be Productive?</a></li>                    <li><a href="#developer-profile-life-outside-work-how-often-do-developers-exercise" role="tab" data-toggle="tab">How Often Do Developers Exercise?</a></li>            </ul>        </div>    </div>    <div class="tab-content">            <div class="tab-pane fade active in" id="developer-profile-life-outside-work-how-often-do-developers-skip-meals-to-be-productive" role="tabpanel">                    <div class="bar-set">                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Never</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 100%;" class="">                        <span>63.6%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">1 - 2 times per week</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 39.6837%;" class="outside">                        <span>25.2%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">3 - 4 times per week</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 9.401%;" class="outside">                        <span>6.0%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Daily or almost every day</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 8.0989%;" class="outside">                        <span>5.2%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>    </div>        <sub class="_muted _line-top">            71,946 responses        </sub>            </div>            <div class="tab-pane fade" id="developer-profile-life-outside-work-how-often-do-developers-exercise" role="tabpanel">                    <div class="bar-set">                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">I don&#39;t typically exercise</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 100%;" class="">                        <span>37.4%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">1 - 2 times per week</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 77.5403%;" class="outside">                        <span>29.0%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">3 - 4 times per week</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 53.0394%;" class="outside">                        <span>19.9%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Daily or almost every day</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 36.5364%;" class="outside">                        <span>13.7%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>    </div>        <sub class="_muted _line-top">            72,108 responses        </sub>            </div>    </div><p>Developers tell us they do not often skip meals because of their workload, and a majority say they exercise at least some. Over 60% of respondents exercise at least weekly, but the most often chosen exercise frequency is 'never'.</p>                                            </div>                </section> </a>                                <p class="_lead">                                    The tools of the trade                                </p>                            </div>                        </div>                    </div>                    <div class="section-content"><div class="subsection-head" id="most-popular-technologies">    <h3 class="_inline-block">        <svg id="Layer_1" Python has risen in the ranks, surpassing C# this year, much like it surpassed PHP last year. Python has a solid claim to being the <a href="https://stackoverflow.blog/2017/09/06/incredible-growth-python/">fastest-growing major programming language</a>.</p><p>We see close alignment in the technology choices of professional developers and the developer population overall.</p>    <h4 id="technology-frameworks-libraries-and-tools"><a with it        </sub>            </div>    </div><p>For the third year in a row, Rust is the most loved programming language among our respondents, followed close behind by Kotlin, a language we asked about for the first time on our survey this year. This means that proportionally, more developers want to continue working with these than other languages.</p><p>Also for the third year in a row, Visual Basic 6 ranks as the most dreaded programming language. Most dreaded means that a high percentage of developers who are currently using the technology express no interest in continuing to do so.</p><p>Python is the most wanted language for the second year in a row, meaning that it is the language that developers who do not yet use it most often say they want to learn.</p>    <h4 differences in tool choices by developer type and role. Developers who write code for mobile apps are more likely to choose Android Studio and Xcode, the most popular choice by DevOps and sysadmins is Vim, and data scientists are more likely to work in IPython/Jupyter, PyCharm, and RStudio.</p>    <h4 id="technology-developers-primary-operating-systems"><a href="#technology-developers-primary-operating-systems">Developers&#39; Primary Operating with median salaries above $70,000 USD. There are regional variations in which languages are associated with the highest pay. Erlang and Scala developers in the US are among the highest paid, while Clojure, Erlang, and Haskell developers earn the most in India.</p><div class="subsection-head" id="correlated-technologies"> id="technology-how-technologies-are-connected"><a href="#technology-how-technologies-are-connected">How Technologies Are Connected</a></h4>        <img src="https://cdn.sstatic.net/insights/Img/Survey/2018/tech_network-1.svg?v=4e6640499a6c" style="width: 100%;" /><p>Technologies cluster together into related ecosystems that tend to be used by the same developers. In this chart we see a large central cluster for web development (with JavaScript, HTML, and CSS) connected via SQL to one for Microsoft technologies (with C#, Visual Studio, and .NET Core). Along the left we see a constellation connecting Java, Android, and iOS across to Linux, bash/shell, and Python. Other smaller correlated clusters include Scala/Spark, C/C++, and other smaller technologies that include language-specific IDEs.</p><div class="subsection-head" id="technology-and-society">    <h3 style="fill:none;stroke:#1060e1;stroke-miterlimit:10"/></svg>        <a href="#technology-and-society">Technology and Society</a>    </h3></div>    <h4 id="technology-what-do-developers-think-is-dangerous-and-exciting-about-ai"><a href="#technology-what-do-developers-think-is-dangerous-and-exciting-about-ai">What Do Developers Think Is Dangerous and Exciting About AI?</a></h4>    <div class="tab-container">        <div class="tab-inner-container">            <ul class="nav nav-tabs" role="tablist">                    <li class="active"><a href="#technology-technology-and-society-dangerous" role="tab" data-toggle="tab">Dangerous</a></li>                    <li><a href="#technology-technology-and-society-exciting" role="tab" data-toggle="tab">Exciting</a></li>            </ul>        </div>    </div>    <div class="tab-content">            <div class="tab-pane fade active in" id="technology-technology-and-society-dangerous" role="tabpanel">                    <div class="bar-set">                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Algorithms making important decisions</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 100%;" class="">                        <span>28.6%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Artificial intelligence surpassing human intelligence (&quot;the singularity&quot;)</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 97.9188%;" class="">                        <span>28.0%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Evolving definitions of &quot;fairness&quot; in algorithmic versus human decisions</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 83.0077%;" class="">                        <span>23.7%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Increasing automation of jobs</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 69.3227%;" class="outside">                        <span>19.8%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>    </div>        <sub class="_muted _line-top">            63,115 responses        </sub>            </div>            <div class="tab-pane fade" id="technology-technology-and-society-exciting" role="tabpanel">                    <div class="bar-set">                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Increasing automation of jobs</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 100%;" class="">                        <span>40.8%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Algorithms making important decisions</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 57.7204%;" class="outside">                        <span>23.5%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Artificial intelligence surpassing human intelligence (&quot;the singularity&quot;)</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 57.1648%;" class="outside">                        <span>23.3%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Evolving definitions of &quot;fairness&quot; in algorithmic versus human decisions</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 30.4497%;" class="outside">                        <span>12.4%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>    </div>        <sub class="_muted _line-top">            65,367 responses        </sub>            </div>    </div><p>Some types of developers are involved in the increasing role of machine learning and artificial intelligence in the world today, so we asked developers what they think is dangerous and exciting about these technologies. There is not much consensus among developers about what is most dangerous; each answer was chosen roughly equally. The top choice for what is exciting about increasing AI is that jobs can be automated.</p>    <h4 id="technology-who-is-primarily-responsible-for-considering-the-ramifications-of-ai"><a href="#technology-who-is-primarily-responsible-for-considering-the-ramifications-of-ai">Who is Primarily Responsible for Considering the Ramifications of AI?</a></h4>    <div class="bar-set">                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">The developers or the people creating the AI</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 100%;" class="">                        <span>47.8%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">A governmental or other regulatory body</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 58.259%;" class="outside">                        <span>27.9%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Prominent industry leaders</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 34.7232%;" class="outside">                        <span>16.6%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Nobody</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 16.1319%;" class="outside">                        <span>7.7%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>    </div>        <sub class="_muted _line-top">            65,553 responses        </sub><p>Developers are most likely to think that the creators and technologists behind the machine learning and AI algorithms are the ones who are ultimately most responsible for the societal issues surrounding artificial intelligence. About a quarter of respondents think that a regulatory body should be primarily responsible.</p>    <h4 id="technology-how-do-developers-feel-about-the-future-of-ai"><a href="#technology-how-do-developers-feel-about-the-future-of-ai">How Do Developers Feel About the Future of AI?</a></h4>    <div class="bar-set">                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">I&#39;m excited about the possibilities more than worried about the dangers.</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 100%;" class="">                        <span>72.8%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">I&#39;m worried about the dangers more than I&#39;m excited about the possibilities.</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 26.134%;" class="outside">                        <span>19.0%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">I don&#39;t care about it, or I haven&#39;t thought about it.</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 11.1988%;" class="outside">                        <span>8.2%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>    </div>        <sub class="_muted _line-top">            69,728 responses        </sub><p>Developers are mostly optimistic about the possibilities that artificial intelligence offers our world, with almost three-fourths of respondents saying that they are overall more excited than worried about the AI future.</p>    <h4 id="technology-ai-concerns-by-developer-type"><a href="#technology-ai-concerns-by-developer-type">AI Concerns by Developer Type</a></h4>        <img src="https://cdn.sstatic.net/insights/Img/Survey/2018/fairness_singular-1.svg?v=9f1f74548620" style="width: 100%;" /><p>The concerns that developers bring to issues around artificial intelligence depend on the kind of coding work they do. For example, data scientists are 1.5 times more likely to consider issues around algorithmic fairness dangerous than any upcoming singularity when computers become more intelligent than people, the most of any kind of developer. We included a free response option on this question; there was not much serious worry about Skynet, but many developers discussed systemic bias being built into algorithmic decision making and the danger of AI being used without the ability to inspect and reason about decision pathways.</p>                                            </div>                </section>                <section developers working part-time. Developers in the United States are somewhat less likely to work as independent contractors or freelancers. In all of these locations, between 70% and 80% of developers are employed full-time.</p>    <h4 id="work-employment-status-for-professional-developers-by-geography"><a   </div><p>Software developers work in a diverse range of industries (so diverse that it's hard to ask about them all in one question!) both inside and outside the technology industry. Our answer choices focused on the tech industry this year, and of these choices, more professional developers work for companies doing web development, IT, and SaaS. Developers working in industries such as consulting and healthcare have more years of professional coding experience. Developers in these industries are twice as likely to have more than 20 years of experience than developers working in web development/design or eCommerce.</p>    <h4 id="work-company-size"><a href="#work-company-size">Company Size</a></h4>    <div class="bar-set">                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Fewer than 10 employees</div>       <span>10.7%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">5,000 to 9,999 employees</div>       <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">10,000 or more employees</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 57.4075%;" class="outside">                        <span>13.6%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>    </div>        <sub class="_muted _line-top">            71,531 responses        </sub><p>Developers work in companies of all sizes, from quite small to large enterprise organizations. More software developers in the United States work at larger companies compared to the rest of the world. The more experienced a developer is, the more likely they are to work at one of the largest companies. A developer with 30 years of experience is twice as likely to work at a company with more than 5,000 employees than a developer with 2 years of experience.</p><div class="subsection-head" <a href="#career-values">Career Values</a>    </h3></div>    <h4 id="work-what-do-developers-hope-to-be-doing-in-five-years"><a href="#work-what-do-developers-hope-to-be-doing-in-five-years">What Do Developers Hope To Be Doing in Five Years?</a></h4>    <div class="bar-set">                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Working in a different or more specialized technical role than the one I&#39;m in now</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 100%;" class="">                        <span>33.9%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Working as a founder or co-founder of my own company</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 75.8257%;" class="outside">                        <span>25.7%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Doing the same work</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 57.419%;" class="outside">                        <span>19.4%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Working as an engineering manager or other functional manager</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 29.1813%;" class="outside">                        <span>9.9%</span>                    </li>                </ul> 19.514%;" class="outside">                        <span>6.6%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div <span>2.8%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Retirement</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 4.9488%;" class="outside">                        <span>1.7%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>    </div>        <sub class="_muted _line-top">            75,718 responses        </sub><p>Developers' career goals are largely focused on technical work, with just over half of respondents saying they want to be in the same or a different technical role in the future. About a quarter of our respondents say they want to start their own company, but this is most common among developers who are younger than 25 years old.</p>    <h4 id="work-how-do-developers-feel-about-their-careers-and-jobs"><a href="#work-how-do-developers-feel-about-their-careers-and-jobs">How Do Developers Feel About Their Careers and Jobs?</a></h4>    <div class="tab-container">        <div class="tab-inner-container">            <ul class="nav nav-tabs" role="tablist">                    <li class="active"><a           </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Moderately satisfied</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 100%;" class="">                        <span>37.5%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row"> satisfied with their career than with their current job. Overall, career satisfaction does not vary significantly by industry. However, current job satisfaction is significantly lower for developers working in financial services and IT. Career satisfaction is highest for older developers, with ages of 50 or higher, and those with 20, 30, or more years of professional experience. Job satisfaction, by contrast, is highest for developers between 35 and 44 years old.</p><div class="subsection-head" id="ethics">    <h3 class="_inline-block">        <svg id="Layer_1" data-name="Layer 1" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 58 52"><title>Ethics</title><line x1="32.26667" y1="10.48802" x2="48.6" y2="1.50469" d="M15.11667,38.25469a5.71667,5.71667,0,0,1-11.43334,0Z" style="fill:none;stroke:#1060e1;stroke-miterlimit:10"/><polyline points="13.483 35.805 13.483 34.171 9.4 24.977 5.317 34.171 5.317 35.805"  <a href="#ethics">Ethics</a>    </h3></div>    <h4 id="work-what-would-developers-do-if-asked-to-write-code-for-an-unethical-purpose"><a href="#work-what-would-developers-do-if-asked-to-write-code-for-an-unethical-purpose">What Would Developers Do If Asked to Write Code for an Unethical Purpose?</a></h4>    <div class="bar-set">                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">No</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 100%;" class="">                        <span>58.5%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Depends on what it is</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 62.5732%;" class="outside">                        <span>36.6%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Yes</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 8.2285%;" class="outside">                        <span>4.8%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>    </div>        <sub class="_muted _line-top">            70,782 responses        </sub><p>When posed with a hypothetical situation where they are asked to write code for a product or purpose that they consider clearly unethical, over half of our respondents say that they would not write such code. Ethical situations can be complicated, and about another third say that it would depend on the situation.</p>    <h4 id="work-how-would-developers-report-ethical-problems-with-code"><a href="#work-how-would-developers-report-ethical-problems-with-code">How Would Developers Report Ethical Problems with Code?</a></h4>    <div class="bar-set">                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Depends on what it is</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 100%;" class="">                        <span>46.6%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Yes, but only within the company</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 76.6793%;" class="outside">                        <span>35.7%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Yes, and publicly</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 28.0386%;" class="outside">                        <span>13.1%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">No</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 9.9172%;" class="outside">                        <span>4.6%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>    </div>        <sub class="_muted _line-top">            70,426 responses        </sub><p>The question of what to do <em>next</em> after an ethical problem has arisen is even more tricky, according to our respondents. The most common answer, from almost half of respondents, is that how to report an ethical problem depends on the particulars of any given situation.</p>    <h4 id="work-who-is-ultimately-most-responsible-for-code-that-accomplishes-something-unethical"><a href="#work-who-is-ultimately-most-responsible-for-code-that-accomplishes-something-unethical">Who Is Ultimately Most Responsible for Code That Accomplishes Something Unethical?</a></h4>    <div class="bar-set">                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Upper management at the company/organization</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 100%;" class="">                        <span>57.5%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">The person who came up with the idea</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 39.6736%;" class="outside">                        <span>22.8%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">The developer who wrote it</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 34.2044%;" class="outside">                        <span>19.7%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>    </div>        <sub class="_muted _line-top">            64,540 responses        </sub><p>Most developers feel that management is ultimately most accountable for unethical results of code. Just under 20% of respondents said that a developer who writes code used for unethical purposes is most responsible.</p>    <h4 id="work-do-developers-have-an-obligation-to-consider-the-ethical-implications-of-their-code"><a href="#work-do-developers-have-an-obligation-to-consider-the-ethical-implications-of-their-code">Do Developers Have an Obligation to Consider the Ethical Implications of Their Code?</a></h4>    <div class="bar-set">                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Yes</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 100%;" class="">                        <span>79.6%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Unsure / I don&#39;t know</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 17.9222%;" class="outside">                        <span>14.3%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">No</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 7.6377%;" class="outside">                        <span>6.1%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>    </div>        <sub class="_muted _line-top">            69,309 responses        </sub><p>Almost 80% of respondents affirm that considering what their code can be used for is the right thing for developers to do. Those who said they were unsure about this were 40% more likely to also say that they do <em>not</em> need to report any ethical problems.</p><p>We included a free response opportunity after this question, and we saw thoughtful reflections from developers. These include responses about how the tools developers build are powerful and come with a lot of responsibility, situations where unethical outcomes may accidentally arise, and how large teams are involved in building software but developers can be the last line of defense against unethical code.</p><div class="subsection-head" id="looking-for-a-job">    <h3 class="_inline-block">        <svg id="Layer_1" data-name="Layer 1" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 47 49"><title>Looking-for-a-Job</title><rect x="5.36283" y="11.94692" width="18.74288" height="15.85936"   </ul>            </div>    </div>        <sub class="_muted _line-top">            24,211 responses; % of respondents who used each word        </sub>            </div>    </div><p>We asked developers on Stack Overflow what they find annoying, exhausting, interesting, and exciting about the process of searching for a new job in separate free response questions. Respondents said the positive aspects of searching for a new job include the new opportunities, technologies, and people that a new position can offer. On the other hand, they expressed frustration with broken processes around interviews and recruiting.</p><div class="subsection-head" id="job-priorities">    <h3 class="_inline-block">        <svg 8.6384%;" class="outside">                        <span>2.6%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>    </div>        <sub class="_muted _line-top">            66,984 responses; % of respondents who chose each option as their lowest priority        </sub>            </div>    </div><p>In general, developers' top priority in assessing a job is compensation, followed by the specific technologies that they will work with. The tech industry is struggling overall with issues around diversity, and individual developers are not making it a priority when looking for a job.</p>    <h4 developers are compensated with salary and benefits work differently across the world, so developer responses vary by geography. Health insurance is prioritized in countries without a national healthcare system (like the United States), and computer equipment allowances are unusually important to developers in India and the UK.</p><div class="subsection-head" id="development-practices">    <h3 class="_inline-block">        <svg id="Layer_1" data-name="Layer 1" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg" viewBox="0 0 53 </sub>            </div>    </div><p>Git is the dominant choice for version control for developers today, with almost 90% of developers checking in their code via Git.</p>    <h4 Median of 13,498 responses; USD        </sub>            </div>    </div><p>Engineering managers, DevOps specialists, and data scientists command the highest salaries. See our <a href="https://insights.stackoverflow.com/survey/2018#methodology">Methodology</a> section for information on how we converted local currencies used by respondents to U.S. dollars.</p><p>Average top earners vary by geography. In India, for example, data scientists are among the top earners, while in European countries, back-end developers and developers working with embedded devices are among the top earners.</p>    <h4 id="work-salary-and-experience-by-developer-type"><a href="#work-salary-and-experience-by-developer-type">Salary and Experience by Developer Type</a></h4>        <img src="https://cdn.sstatic.net/insights/Img/Survey/2018/salary_devtype-1.svg?v=351efb836ca6" style="width: 100%;" /><p>Naturally, developers with more years of experience are paid more. However, we also see that some type of coding work is paid more highly at the same level of experience. Data scientists and DevOps specialists are high earners for their level of experience.</p>    <h4 id="work-salary-and-experience-by-language"><a href="#work-salary-and-experience-by-language">Salary and Experience by Language</a></h4>        <img src="https://cdn.sstatic.net/insights/Img/Survey/2018/salary_language-1.svg?v=695ac080e941" style="width: 100%;" /><p>Developers using languages that appear above the line in this chart, such as Go, Clojure, and F#, are being paid more even given how much experience they have. Developers using languages below the line, like PHP and Visual Basic 6, however, are paid less even given years of experience. The size of the circles in this chart represents how many developers are using that language compared to the others.</p><div class="section-intro  content-cta">    <div class="section-intro-content We asked a traditional <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Net_Promoter">net promoter score</a> question for Stack Overflow as a whole and our NPS is 75, a world class score according to style="fill:none;stroke:#1060e1;stroke-miterlimit:10"/></g></svg>        <a href="#developer-opinions-on-ads">Developer Opinions on Ads</a>    </h3></div>    <h4 id="community-how-do-developers-feel-about-ads"><a href="#community-how-do-developers-feel-about-ads">How Do Developers Feel About Ads?</a></h4>    <div class="bar-set">                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">I enjoy seeing online updates from companies that I like</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 100%;" class="">                        <span>3.4</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">Online advertising can be valuable when it is relevant to me</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 99.0297%;" class="">                        <span>3.3</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">I fundamentally dislike the concept of advertising</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 95.5758%;" class="">                        <span>3.2</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>    </div>        <sub class="_muted _line-top">            74,710 responses; agreement on a 1-5 scale, from strongly disagree to strongly agree        </sub><p>Like many websites, Stack Overflow has ads, and we want to know how to make our ads more relevant for our users. Over half of our respondents agreed or strongly agreed that they enjoy seeing online updates from companies they like and that online advertising can be valuable when it is relevant. About 40% of developers say they fundamentally dislike the concept of advertising.</p>    <h4 id="community-ad-priorities-for-developers"><a href="#community-ad-priorities-for-developers">Ad Priorities for Developers</a></h4>    <div class="tab-container">        <div class="tab-inner-container">            <ul class="nav nav-tabs" role="tablist">                    <li class="active"><a href="#community-developer-opinions-on-ads-highest-priority" role="tab" data-toggle="tab">Highest Priority</a></li>                    <li><a href="#community-developer-opinions-on-ads-lowest-priority" role="tab" data-toggle="tab">Lowest Priority</a></li>            </ul>        </div>    </div>    <div class="tab-content">            <div class="tab-pane fade active in" id="community-developer-opinions-on-ads-highest-priority" role="tabpanel">                    <div class="bar-set">                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">The advertisement is relevant to me</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 100%;" class="">                        <span>38.8%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">The advertisement provides useful information</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 36.4422%;" class="outside">                        <span>14.1%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">The advertisement seems trustworthy</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 35.4579%;" class="outside">                        <span>13.8%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">The advertisement is honest about its goals</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 33.3701%;" class="outside">                        <span>12.9%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">The advertisement is from a company that I like</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 23.8177%;" class="outside">                        <span>9.2%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">The advertisement avoids fluffy or vague language</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 15.3514%;" class="outside">                        <span>6.0%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">The advertisement offers something of value, like a free trial</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 13.2466%;" class="outside">                        <span>5.1%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>    </div>        <sub class="_muted _line-top">            60,479 responses; % of respondents who chose each option as their highest priority        </sub>            </div>            <div class="tab-pane fade" id="community-developer-opinions-on-ads-lowest-priority" role="tabpanel">                    <div class="bar-set">                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">The advertisement offers something of value, like a free trial</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 100%;" class="">                        <span>32.5%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">The advertisement avoids fluffy or vague language</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 77.5565%;" class="outside">                        <span>25.2%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">The advertisement is from a company that I like</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 51.5159%;" class="outside">                        <span>16.7%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">The advertisement seems trustworthy</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 25.7757%;" class="outside">                        <span>8.4%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">The advertisement is honest about its goals</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 24.1758%;" class="outside">                        <span>7.8%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">The advertisement is relevant to me</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 15.8355%;" class="outside">                        <span>5.1%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">The advertisement provides useful information</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 13.2776%;" class="outside">                        <span>4.3%</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>    </div>        <sub class="_muted _line-top">            60,478 responses; % of respondents who chose each option as their lowest priority        </sub>            </div>    </div><p>In general, developers' top priority in assessing an advertisement is whether it's relevant to them, followed by whether it provides useful information and is trustworthy. Developers are not swayed by free offers in advertisements.</p><div class="section-intro  content-cta">    <div class="section-intro-content content-cta-container">        <div </div><p>Most of the respondents to our survey consider themselves part of our community, but this varies for different groups of people. For example, we find that respondents who identify as male see themselves as part of the community at higher rates than those with other gender identities. The tech community as a whole, and we at Stack Overflow in particular, still have work to do in this area.</p>    <h4 id="community-interest-in-hypothetical-new-tools-on-stack-overflow"><a href="#community-interest-in-hypothetical-new-tools-on-stack-overflow">Interest in Hypothetical New Tools on Stack Overflow</a></h4>    <div class="bar-set">                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">An employer or job review system</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 100%;" class="">                        <span>3.2</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">An area for Q&amp;A related to career growth</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 99.5222%;" class="">                        <span>3.2</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">A programming-oriented blog platform</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 92.5076%;" class="">                        <span>3.0</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">A peer mentoring system</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 87.6292%;" class="">                        <span>2.8</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>                <div class="bar-row">                    <div class="bar-label">A private area for people new to programming</div>                    <ul>                    <li style="width: 82.2137%;" class="">                        <span>2.6</span>                    </li>                </ul>            </div>    </div>        <sub class="_muted _line-top">            70,687 responses; interest on a 1-5 scale, from not at all interested to extremely interested        </sub><p>As we work to make our community a better place for developers to learn, share, and grow their careers, we asked our survey respondents about their interest in possible new tools. An employer review system and help with career growth garnered the most interest.</p>    <h4 id="community-what-words-do-developers-use-to-describe-stack-overflow"><a of respondents who used each word        </sub>            </div>    </div><p>In these free response questions, we asked developers first to describe the Stack Overflow community in general, and then what they would change about it. Developers were largely positive about Stack Overflow, focusing on the helpful nature of the community, and specifically had ideas about how questions, answers, comments, and reputation are handled. The treatment of new users and new people in our community were mentioned often as well.</p>    <h4 id="community-developers-perspectives-about-our-community"><a href="#community-developers-perspectives-about-our-community">Developers&#39; Perspectives About Our Community</a></h4>        <img src="https://cdn.sstatic.net/insights/Img/Survey/2018/positive_negative-1.svg?v=fe7689f8c4e9" style="width: 100%;" /><p>This year, our survey included questions about what developers think the best, worst, most annoying, and most exciting things about Stack Overflow are. (These questions were randomized so that each respondent got one positive and one negative version.) In the positive versions of these questions, respondents were more likely to talk about the wealth of sharing and collaboration on our site. In the negative versions, respondents reflected on harsh interactions they've witnessed, downvotes, and handling of duplicate questions.</p><div class="section-intro  content-cta">    <div
