                            <a href="#methodology">                                    <h2 class="_orange">                                        Methodology                                    </h2>                                </a>                                <p class="_lead">                                    How we planned and analyzed our survey                                </p>                            </div>                        </div>                    </div>                    <div class="section-content">                            <p>This report is based on a survey of 101,592 software developers from 183 countries around the world. This number of responses are what we consider “qualified” for analytical purposes based on completion and time spent on the survey; another approximately 20,000 responses were started but not included in the analysis because respondents did not answer enough questions. Of the qualified responses, 67,441 (66.4%) completed the entire survey.</p>                            <h3 class="_lead"> Qualified Responses Worldwide</h3>                            <table class="table table-bordered">                                <tbody>                                    <tr>                                        <td>Europe</td>                                        <td>39,001</td>                                    </tr>                                    <tr>                                        <td>North America</td>                                        <td>25,016</td>                                    </tr>                                    <tr>                                        <td>Asia</td>                                        <td>24,700</td>                                    </tr>                                    <tr>                                        <td>South America</td>                                        <td>4,162</td>                                    </tr>                                    <tr>                                        <td>Africa</td>                                        <td>2,869</td>                                    </tr>                                    <tr>                                        <td>Australia/Oceania</td>                                        <td>2,591</td>                                    </tr>                                    <tr>                                        <td>Other (country not listed)</td>                                        <td>84</td>                                    </tr>                                </tbody>                            </table>                            <br />                            <ul>                                <li>The survey was fielded from January 8 to January 28.</li>                                <li>The median time spent on the survey for qualified responses was 25.8 minutes, and the median time for those who finished the entire survey was 29.4 minutes.</li>                                <li>Respondents were recruited primarily through channels owned by Stack Overflow. The top 5 sources of respondents were banner ads, email lists, house ads, blog posts, and Twitter.  Since respondents were recruited in this way, highly engaged users on Stack Overflow were more likely to notice the links for the survey and click to begin it. Respondents who finished the survey were awarded a “Census” badge as a motivation to complete the survey.</li>                                <li>We treated responses as qualified for analysis if the user spent a certain amount of time relative to how far they got into the survey. Most survey responses that spent less than 5 minutes were excluded from the final sample.</li>                                <li>                                    We asked respondents about their salary. First, we asked what currency each respondent typically used. Then we asked that respondent what their salary was in that currency, and whether that salary was weekly, monthly, or yearly.                                    <ul>                                        <li>For a short time on the first day, there was a bug that left out the last part of the question (weekly vs. monthly vs. yearly); those salary responses are not included here.</li>                                        <li>We converted salaries from user currencies to USD using the exchange rate on 2018-01-18, and also converted to annual salaries assuming 12 working months and 50 working weeks.</li>                                        <li>This question, like most on the survey, was optional. There were 58,650 respondents (57.7% of qualified respondents) who gave us salary data.</li>                                        <li>The top approximately 1% of salaries inside and outside of the US were trimmed and replaced with threshold values. The threshold values for inside and outside the US were different.</li>                                    </ul>                                </li>                                <li>Many questions were only shown to respondents based on their previous answers. For example, questions about jobs and work were only shown to those who said they were working in a job.</li>                                <li>The questions were organized into several blocks of questions, which were randomized in order. Also, the answers to most questions were randomized in order.</li>                                <li>Due to an error, Oracle and SQLite were excluded from the question about databases for the first day of the survey. We carefully examined whether the results for the other databases changed from the first day compared to the rest of the survey fielding period and they did not. The results shown here for database use and most loved/dreaded/wanted databases only use responses from after Oracle and SQLite were added to the possible answers.</li>                                <li>On 2018-3-19, we made some edits to this site based on community feedback to address two issues: a) how we handled the responses of transgender developers, to avoid implying that being a transgender man or woman is a separate gender and b) a higher level of clarity throughout the discussion about our survey sample and its limitations.</li>                            </ul>                                            </div>                </section>            <section id="cta">                <div class="section-intro">                    <div class="row section-intro-content">                        <div class="col-md-12 col-sm-6 col-xs-12">                            <div>                                <div class="cta-share _small">                                    <span class="_bold">Share This</span><a id="share-fb" href="#" title="share on Facebook"><i class="fa fa-lg fa-facebook-square _fb-blue"></i></a><a id="share-tw" href="#" title="share on Twitter"><i class="fa fa-lg fa-twitter-square _twitter-blue"></i></a><a id="share-gp" href="#" title="share on Google+"><i class="fa fa-lg fa-google-plus-square _google-plus-red"></i></a><script>    $(function () {        function pop(uri, name, options) {            if (!window.open(uri, name, options)) {                window.location.href = uri;
